Tim HeuerSunday, November 15, 2009 at 9:13pm EST

You can use the ASPNET db as well if you'd like -- that's what is set up out of the box with the RIA services project templates. If you have your own scheme, you can inherit from AuthenticationBase and do what you need in those classes. ASPNET authentication isn't just for SQLExpress though -- you can use it on full SQL server or write your own custom database provider that maps to the API for authentication and membership within ASPNET.

Facebook User, Jonathan Moore
Facebook UserTuesday, August 16, 2011 at 3:23am EDT

At http://biolod.org/readme you can find useful information to help understand the terms used in BioLOD.org, and other helpful advice. Database A "Database" is a data space that constructs a separated and independent data set. "Database" is symbolized by the 'disk' icon. Class "Class" defines a set of RDF individuals. "Class" is symbolized by the 'table' icon. Instance "Instance" corresponds to each RDF individual. "Instance" is symbolized by the 'paper' icon. Property "Property" in BioLOD.org is compatible with a property in RDF/OWL. A property itself is described with pre-defined properties including URI, name, description. Best Regards, BioLOD.org

Facebook UserMonday, May 9, 2011 at 7:53pm EDT

After a fantastic nearly 19 years at Macromedia/Adobe, I've made the difficult decision to leave the company I've called home for so long. Living out my entrepreneurial dreams is something that has been on my mind for many years and the perfect opportunity has come up to turnaround a startup in the consumer/media space with some ex-Macromedia folks here in San Francisco. My last startup adventure turned out to be Macromedia in 1992 and keeping fingers crossed we have a similar successful outcome! During my fortunate time here, I've had the amazing honor of working with so many smart, fun and talented people who have worked hard to achieve so much. With many of you I've seen multimedia in computers go mainstream, the advent of the web, the multimedia-fication of the web with Shockwave, created the Flash Platform as one of the "founding fathers", pursued new mobile business opportunities for the emerging "smart phone" market in Europe and kicked off a concerted effort to provide developers services beyond the box. Hard to imagine having all those experiences in one career let alone only half of one. We are in an exciting, transformational time in the industry once again and there are many opportunities that exist. To my Adobe family, with all the amazing technology assets and talented people, there will continue to be major opportunities to pursue. To others with whom I've worked with and where friendships have emerged, looking forward to finding other ways to work together and expand the great things we've already done together. I sincerely wish you the very best and look forward to the next time our paths cross again. My last day will be Thursday, May 12. As tradition states, there will be a going away bash at Mars Bar (798 Brannan Street) on Wednesday, May 11 (kicking off around 4pm). I look forward to raising a glass with you. Here are ways to connect with me moving forward: LinkedIn: http://www.linkedin.com/in/ericjwittman Email: eric.wittman@gmail.com Mobile: +1-415-516-2655 All the best, Eric

Juniper Networks, Jonathan Moore
Juniper NetworksWednesday, May 4, 2011 at 3:04pm EDT

Join us on May 24th at 11:00 AM to find out you can simplify your network. Register at https://learningportal.juniper.net/juniper/user_activity_schedule_info.aspx?id=17677&activity=4797. In order to achieve a Simply Connected campus, the wired network must be simplified. New Virtual Chassis capability on the EX8200 and EX4500 Series Ethernet Switches enable you to simplify the network while increasing resiliency. Virtual Chassis technology not only reduces the number of managed devices, but also improves network performance by removing looping protocols from the network. This session will describe how the technology works.

Hey Jonathan! You may assume it is spam but it's not. I just saw your comment on techcrunch and figured you'd probably like to hear about ark. ark.com is a new website that allows you to earn funds for your causes just by browsing or shopping online all for free. They've basically got agreements with sites like google, amazon, e-bay, livingsocial etc. so that every time you use them from ark.com, you can earn money for any cause you want. Yea, it's been done before but never like this. You should check it out. http://ark.com/ Peace! Noemi

The next generation of the ASCOM Platform provides compatibility with Windows 7 User Account Control and 64-bit systems, some new device interfaces, and even more support for both drivers and astronomy applications. It contains new simulators, updated Visual Studio driver templates, and much more. This huge project is nearing completion with several people working on it, and is expected to be available in May 2011. An absolute requirement for Platform 6 is that it be 100% compatible with existing astronomy software and drivers. It is currently being tested by driver and application developerws to make sure this requirement is met. For details see the URL below. http://ascom-standards.org/About/Projects.htm

About the speaker: Dr. Meagley is presently CEO, CTO and resident "Mad Scientist" at ONE Nano, a company founded to invent, develop and market photonic nanodevices and device arrays for biomarker characterization and related technology. Prior to forming ONE Nanotechnologies and following post-doctoral research at UC-Berkeley and Cornell, Rob was Principle Investigator, Senior Staff Scientist, and the Molecules for Advanced Patterning Program Manager for Intel. In 2004 he was named Researcher-In Residence for a group he created at Lawrence Berkeley National Labs to discover, develop and commercialize advanced lithography materials. With over 38 papers, 41 patents, and numerous awards to his name, Rob is an expert in the design and synthesis of small molecules and complex molecular systems. In addition to managing several complex, interdisciplinary teams and research programs, he has also lectured extensively on materials science chemistry and nanotechnology, and provides consulting services to the nanotechnology, MEMS and biotechnology communities.

Scientific AmericanSunday, April 10, 2011 at 7:38pm EDT

Join us at 2 pm Eastern on Monday on Scientific American's Facebook page for a live chat with award-winning science and medical writer Maryn McKenna. McKenna wrote "The Enemy Within: A New Pattern of Antibiotic Resistance," for the April 2011 issue of SA. The article focuses on a resistance-conferring gene in Klebsiella pneumoniae, a bacterium that in hospitalized patients is one of the most frequent causes of pneumonia and bloodstream infection (http://www.scientificamerican.com/article.cfm?id=the-enemy-within). McKenna is also the author of "Superbug: The Fatal Menace of MRSA," (http://www.amazon.com/Superbug-Fatal-Menace-Maryn-McKenna/dp/B0048ELEUO/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1302478522&sr=8-1).

Sierra Sciences, Jonathan Moore
Sierra SciencesThursday, September 9, 2010 at 1:05pm EDT

RENO, Nev., Sept 08, 2010 /PRNewswire via COMTEX/ -- Sierra Sciences, in collaboration with TA Sciences, Geron Corporation, PhysioAge, and the Spanish National Cancer Research Center (CNIO), has announced the first compound ever discovered that activates the enzyme telomerase in the human body - a critical prerequisite for technology that could arrest or reverse the aging process in humans. This compound is a natural product derived nutraceutical known as TA-65. These findings appear as a research article entitled 'A natural product telomerase activator as part of a health maintenance program,' published September 7, 2010 ahead of print in the peer-reviewed journal Rejuvenation Research. The article can be found at http://www.liebertonline.com/doi/abs/10.1089/rej.2010.1085. Researchers discovered that TA-65 was associated with a statistically significant "age-reversal" effect in the immune system, in that it led to declines in the percentage of senescent cytotoxic T cells and natural killer cells after six to twelve months of use. In addition, further analysis with automated high-throughput confocal microscopy (HT-qFISH) revealed a decline in the percentage of white blood cells with critically short telomeres after twelve to eighteen months of use. Several peer-reviewed publications have calculated that humans have a theoretical maximum lifespan of 125 years, but our health declines long before that. Many scientists believe that this limit on lifespan and decline in health is imposed by the gradual shortening of our telomeres, structures at the ends of our chromosomes that shorten with every cell division. Telomere shortening is thought to be the "clock of aging" contained within the human body. It has been repeatedly demonstrated that a human cell that does not undergo telomere shortening will divide indefinitely and is, by all available measurements, immortal. The publication reports that TA-65 can cause telomerase, an enzyme that lengthens telomeres, to become active in human cells. Telomerase activation by TA-65 was shown to lengthen the shortest telomeres in humans, potentially extending human lifespan and healthspan. Telomerase activation is thought to be a keystone of future regenerative medicine and a necessary condition for clinical immortality. Although TA-65 is probably too weak to completely arrest the aging process, it is the first telomerase activator recognized as safe for human use. "We are on the cusp of curing aging," said William Andrews, Ph.D., co-author of this study and President and CEO of Sierra Sciences, LLC. "TA-65 is going to go down in history as the first supplement you can take that doesn't merely extend your life a few years by improving your health, but actually affects the underlying mechanisms of aging. Better telomerase inducers will be developed in the coming years, but TA-65 is the first of a whole new family of telomerase-activating therapies that could eventually keep us young and healthy forever." Telomerase activation has potential medical applications beyond extending human lifespan. Epidemiological studies have shown that short telomeres in humans are a risk factor for diseases including, among others, atherosclerosis, diabetes, Alzheimer's, and cancer. The present study also reports encouraging news on the effect of TA-65 on the body's immune system. Infectious diseases lead to telomere shortening in the immune system, as immune cells divide to fight infections. Telomerase activation should prevent this telomere shortening and allow the body's immune system to fight a chronic infection indefinitely. The present study on TA-65 lends support to this hypothesis. In individuals infected with CMV, a virus which prematurely ages the immune system and significantly reduces life expectancy, TA-65 caused an apparent "age reversal" of approximately 5 to 20 years based on one biomarker of immune aging. For the same reason, telomerase activation is a potential treatment for AIDS. "We tend to see HIV turning into AIDS when the cells of the immune system develop critically short telomeres," said Andrews. "HIV can essentially cause the immune system to die of old age while the majority of the body is still young. A telomerase activator could theoretically prevent an HIV-positive individual from ever developing AIDS."

Sierra SciencesWednesday, September 8, 2010 at 4:25pm EDT

Dear Friends: I am writing you because Sierra Sciences has suffered a sudden and unexpected loss of funding. We need $200,000 per month to keep the company operating until mid-2011, when we expect to become self-sufficient with revenue from product sales. Sierra Sciences is poised to make world-altering breakthroughs in anti-aging medicine. It is no exaggeration to say that we are on the brink of actually curing the disease we call aging! Unfortunately, our current investors were both hit hard by the financial crisis. They can no longer maintain the funding that drives Sierra Sciences‚Äô research. Looking ahead, Sierra Sciences‚Äô management realizes that in the current economic climate we will have to generate our funding ourselves. To this end, we have formed an alliance with a well-known and very successful manufacturer and retailer of natural products. They will be marketing our discoveries as anti-aging nutraceuticals. This alliance is expected to bring us enough revenue to support further nutraceutical research by mid-2011, and to support pharmaceutical research by mid-2012. Yesterday, Sierra Sciences‚Äô two investors informed me that they will soon cease all funding of the company. Without interim funding, we will lose not only our opportunity to profit from the nutraceutical market, but also our opportunity to develop our pharmaceutical discoveries into a cure for aging. This would be a tragedy for humanity, as well as a missed opportunity to create a multi-billion dollar industry. The bottom line is that Sierra Sciences needs $200,000 per month as soon as possible. We will need this interim funding for 6-12 months, at which time we expect to become self-sufficient from nutraceutical sales. This investment would buy the investor significant ownership of the company. My current investors have also mentioned that they would consider selling some or all of their equity stake in Sierra Sciences. They are still very interested in curing aging and still strongly believe in Sierra Sciences‚Äô path. Together, they have invested just over $20 million and own a controlling interest in the company. They would welcome a conversation on this subject. Please contact me if you would like to learn more about our situation. All my contact information is included with my signature below. Facebook UserWednesday, May 26, 2010 at 9:23am EDT

We're thrilled to announce an exciting new feature on Hohm: starting today, nearly 60 million homes in the United States will have a ‚ÄúHohm Score,‚Äù our instant estimate of a home‚Äôs energy efficiency. The Hohm Score is a 1-to-100 estimated score- with 100 being the best- that we calculate for each of the homes in our database. Each Hohm score is unique in that it compares a specific home's estimated and potential energy efficiency. To create a Hohm Score, we combine our own algorithms with public record information and advanced analytics licensed from Lawrence Berkeley National Laboratory and the Department of Energy to create a personalized Hohm experience, including money saving recommendations. Facebook User, Jonathan Moore
Facebook UserWednesday, March 10, 2010 at 10:05am EST

Hi again, all. Sarah and I are starting work on the poster session proposal and I'm looking for potential participants now. The broad topic is food and health, and should relate in some way to the meeting theme of "circulation." Topics that immediately come to my mind are the origins of agriculture, food sharing, forager-farmer interactions, cash cropping and export economies, famine and food security, urban food deserts, mixed economies (e.g. horticulture and wage labor), ethnobotany and trade in traditional medicine, and refrigerated shipping/trucking. Obviously, this topic could take us in a number of directions. We're looking for posters from any subfield of anthropology and welcome submissions from both students and faculty, though student participation is highly encouraged. This is what the AAA website has to say about "circulation:" "We can think in terms of circulation across time as well as space, through different organizing principles, and in a variety of shapes and forms." "The idea of circulation invites us to consider what triggers, facilitates, constrains, disrupts or stops flows; what is at stake in these processes, and for whom; and what their consequences might be for humans and for the environment. It opens up questions about what exactly circu¬≠lates: signs, objects or bodies. Do different things circulate in different ways? Do they change or remain constant? What new phenomena, arrangements and inequalities does circula¬≠tion produce? How are resources and ways of understanding them identified, made sense of, produced and distributed in the process? How and why do rates and types of circulation vary across time and space? What crystallizes and what continues to flow and reshape?" So, if you have an idea for a poster that you'd like to present please send me an abstract by Monday if you can. I need a total of 7 participants. You can send your abstract to me at cnp304@mail.missouri.edu or here on Facebook if that is easier. Regards, Christina Pomianek PS, If you've never presented a poster before, here is some information from the AAA website about poster session and submission guidelines: FEAR NOT THE POSTER Agustin Fuentes Notre Dame U For some reason, many anthropologists avoid the poster as a viable and effective means of presenting their work. I think we anthropologists are a bit misguided in our general lack of enthusiasm for the poster presentation. The poster presents an interactive, visual medium for conveying our research, theory and practice. We need to realize that we have imposed an unspoken caste system on conference presentations, and placed posters on a lower rung. This system must be overthrown. Here are five reasons why: Great visibility for your work: A more diverse group of people will see your work as a poster than if it is tucked away in a specialized session that only the presenters attend. Our Annual Meetings are huge, and seeing more than just a few presentations can be very difficult. If the poster session location is decent and your poster well-designed, you will attract not only those seeking your poster out, but also passers-by and others who may never have otherwise had the opportunity to see your presentation ¬∑ Time to interact with the audience/peers: Unlike the podium session, you actually get to chat with those interested in your work. The format and time allotted to posters facilitates a broader discourse in the moment. No more 15 minutes and out . . . here you actually have the time to elaborate, discuss and engage in academic exchange, rather than just preaching from the podium. ¬∑ Dissemination of supplemental information: The venue and format of poster presentations allow for the easy distribution of manuscripts, related articles, utilization of video and even websites. You can easily bring reprints or even set up a laptop or VCR/TV to enhance the information presented in the poster. Posters can be a gateway to connections, student interest and collegial collaboration (which is pretty much the purpose for presenting in the first place). ¬∑ You can always see the poster: Unlike the problems of ‚Äúlow talkers,‚Äù broken microphones and poor acoustics that frequent podium sessions, a well-presented poster always is accessible. Clear fonts, images and graphics allow the audience to absorb the information at their pace and engage the presenter directly with questions, compliments or relevant issues. ¬∑ Poster sessions always run on time: One of the main drawbacks to AAA Annual Meetings is running across gargantuan lobbies and labyrinth-like hallways in search of strangely named rooms with the session you want to see, only to arrive and find that it is running 47 minutes late. Poster sessions run on time and allow for a casual perusal of the presentations. No more sneaking out the back and knocking over the slide projector. Poster presentations let you plan your visit accordingly, and you can come and go without embarrassing moments! In addition to these five main points, posters also can be a valuable means of presenting multiauthored work, especially with projects that incorporate students. For students, a poster can be an important introduction to professional presentations and give them a chance to engage in public academic discourse prior to attempting a podium presentation.

Facebook User, Jonathan Moore
Facebook UserWednesday, September 3, 2008 at 7:15pm EDT

Facebook Pages are a powerful way to reach a mass audience and their friends. Sometimes, however, you‚Äôll want to limit who sees what. Here are three tools to help: (1) Age Restrictions for Pages: You can restrict your Page to users over age 13, 17, 18, 19, or 21, or the legal drinking age where they live. On your Page‚Äôs edit page, scroll down to ‚ÄúSettings‚Äù at the bottom. (2) Targeted Messaging: When you send a message to fans, you can target it by geography, gender, and age. For example, a musician can promote a concert to fans in the area. When sending an update, check the ‚ÄúTarget this update‚Äù box. (3) New FBML Tags: If you use FBML (http://www.new.facebook.com/apps/application.php?id=4949752878), you can restrict content by country and age. For example, if you have licensed content for U.S. and Canada users only, you can to restrict it to those countries, and show alternative content to other users. More details are on the Facebook Developers Blog: http://developers.facebook.com/news.php?blog=1&story=150.

In addition, your Facebook Page is automatically listed in the alphabetized Pages Directory: http://www.facebook.com/directory/pages. Your fans and customers can use the Directory to browse or search for your business even if they‚Äôre not logged in to Facebook.

Facebook UserSaturday, March 22, 2008 at 1:52am EDT

If you have enabled Video on your Facebook Page, fans can now add videos to it. To control fan video settings, click "Edit Settings" in the lower "fan videos" box of the Video player on your Page. The choices are yours when it comes to your Facebook Page. You have control over how fans can contribute photos, video, discussion topics, and more, to your Page. By letting fans join in the conversation, you help them serve as your digital street team. Every contribution they make to your Page can generate News Feed stories to their friends, expanding your reach.

Facebook Pages have some new features available for you: 1. User Photo Uploads Now, your fans will be able to upload photos to your Facebook Page...if you let them. Go to your Facebook Page and Edit on the Photos box to turn on this feature. All New Pages will have this feature pre-enabled upon creation. 2. Dynamic Content in the Profile Box You can now replace the main picture on your Facebook Page with dynamic content using either the Flash or FBML applications. Just install either of these applicaitons (find them at www.facebook.com/facebookpages and then select the flash/fbml option when you choose to edit your profile picture.) 3. Legal Drinking Age Settings If you are a bar or alcohol company, you can adjust age settings to meet legal drinking age requirements by clicking edit on your Facebook page, and scrolling down to the settings box. 4.
